< Review>
For kosher pizza, it's pretty good. Compared to non kosher pizza, it's bland and expensive. Other foods are generally pretty good. Large selection of vegetarian foods, including Mexican, Greek salad, stuffed pretzels and desserts. Order at the counter and they'll bring you the food, but that's about all the service you'll get. They won't check on you, and if it's crowded you'll be lucky even to get a cup of water. Id recommend taking your food to go rather than eating there.<//Review>

< text>
When my grandsons visit me from Long Beach I take them here or another kosher pizza place in the valley.  The other one is so much better.  The price is high at both places but Brami's is skimpy on the cheese whereas the other place is not.  The crust is good.  I am also amazed when I read other reviews that say the service is good.  We have never had good service when we come here.
We decided on our last trip that it is worth driving a little further to go to the other kosher pizza place.< /text>

<Date>1552076974219<//Date>< Text>
If I could give this place a higher rating I would. First off they have their own parking lot, which in a city that's known to be hard for finding parking, is amazing. The decorations inside (paintings, pictures, etc) give an authentic and homey feel without feeling like one of those fake Latin restaurants (you know what I'm talking about).

It's a cozy spot with 2 tables for large parties (~8) and about 3 tables for seating 2.

The food was absolutely phenomenal, I had the Cubano. And I haven't had a Cubano that great in a long time. Also comes with chips and salsa. The salsa was flavorful but not spicy.

Will definitely be coming back, the staff was personable & attentive, food was dynamite, free parking, great atmosphere.<//Text>

< Text>
I rented one of their properties in Ocean Beach, San Diego. My review for the house is below. Working with Penny Realty was also a breeze, they were very responsive and there were no issues.

Loved this beach house! I came with my family and it was perfect. There is a ground floor bedroom with walk-in shower that is good for any older people, and suited my 94 year old grandma very well. The other bedrooms are upstairs. The main dining area, living area and downstairs patio has direct views of the sand and waves. We were worried that grandma wouldn't be able to see the waves from the patio because of how broad the beach was, but you are able to see crashing waves so that was great. It is very easy to spend time on the patio and it is pretty spacious, easily fit all 6 of us staying there. There are two TV/living areas in case one part of the house is going to bed earlier than the other. The kitchen was very functional, but if you need things like tin foil and baggies you should bring your own. The beach out front is great, with direct sand access from the patio. When we were there there was a rip current on the beach directly in front of us, but the lifeguards recommended just moving one lifeguard station up. There are about 10 bonfire rings on the beach just in front of and slightly north of the house. We went during grunion run season (pretty prolonged march-august) and there was an amazing turn out on night 3 of the run just to the south of us, between the stone break and the pier, but almost nothing on night 4! Overall, a nice cozy beach house. Not super modern or gonna wow you with style, but definitely clean, put together, thoughtful furniture, and well done.<//Text>

< text>
This is for our Airbnb rental, "Mission Beach Tower #1": Our family had a great mini-vacation here. There were only 3 of us, and I felt like there was enough space to sleep 5-6 comfortably if we wanted. We love to cook, and were happy with all the kitchen amenities. We never felt like we were missing anything. The location is a beach-lovers dream. You have two beaches to choose from, and both are a 5 minute walk away. Either catch some waves on the coast, or enjoy some peace & quiet at Mariners Basin. Belmont Park is also a short walk away, where there are some fun rides, shops, and restaurants. During our stay we went to Seaworld, which was about an 8 minute car ride away (We Uber'd there for about $7), and the Zoo which took about 15 minutes. There is a small market down the street where you can buy most groceries from, otherwise the nearest grocery store (Ralph's) is about a 10 minute drive away. If I had one complaint, it would be that the area isn't the best for families once the sun goes down. Lots of loud drunk college kids throwing house parties, coming in & out of the bars down the block, and hanging around in the street. I asked one of the Market owners if this was a regular thing, and he said it was fairly common on weekends. It was a holiday weekend, so maybe they were more active than usual, but something to be wary of if you enjoy your peace and quiet.<//text>

We had a great time at the Aloha rental from Penny Realty!

I highly recommend working with Penny Realty, they made this experience so easy and carefree! I didn't get into San Diego until very late the night i was supposed to check in, but they worked with me and I was able to sign the rental agreement the next morning. The house slept 6 grown men comfortably, and everything we needed was right there. There are many bars and restaurants within walking distance, and even a Ralph's supermarket- one night we bought groceries and cooked our own dinner! This property isn't next to any other residences, so it was nice and quiet at night, and all of us slept like babies. Not to mention the benefit of having a bike rental shop on one side, and a great Mexican taqueria on the other side. The food from the place next door was delicious!

Everything was very clean. The appliances were modern and well cared for; the linens and bath towels all looked basically brand new and we used them with no reservations! The porch areas are awesome during the mornings to watch the sunrise- the perfect way to start a day in SD!

Of course, this review wouldn't count for anything if I didn't talk about how close Aloha is to the beach- step out the front door, cross Mission Blvd, and in 5 minutes you can dig your toes into the sand! We had a great weekend playing beach football, and a great night walking up and down the boardwalk, watching the waves come in. Talk about a prime location!

Thanks to Penny Realty for coming through in the clutch on our check-in day, and making up for SeaTac's terrible TSA lines. I was stressed until I got to San Diego- from there on out, it was smooth sailing!</Review>

< text>
I have been coming to Dr, Hodes for over 15 years.  After my previous optometrist retired, I struggled to find a good optometrist.  They struggled with my prescription because of my high astigmatism, and as a result my glasses seemed off.  From the first visit to Dr. Hodes, I was completely pleased.  He had not trouble finding an accurate prescription that would correct my vision with both glasses and contacts.  Finding glasses has always been challenging too because the limited options for round faces.  The opticians are amazing.  Every year, they take the time to help me find a nice pair of glasses.  They are honest with questionable picks I have had, and the result is always great!  I have referred friends to Dr. Hodes.
He has been the "second opinion"  and saved a friend from unnecessary surgery (as well as myself by reminding me that corrective vision wouldn't correct my vision 100%).  My annual visit is always completely positive!<//text>

<user>102330294009146773607</user><text>I was looking forward to checking this place out and finally got a chance to stop by here for lunch.
Very nicely designed interior with a bar and outside seating as well. Good choice of beers on tap and a full kitchen.
I ordered what came recommended, which was a sandwich with both turkey and pulled pork as well as a small soup on the side.
Sandwich was quite boring and had more mustard that it needed which, when combined with the pickles resulted in it being too salty and sour with no other taste despite the pulled pork, which according to the staff is cooked in-house. In addition the bread roll was a bit big for the content of the sandwich so I had to remove half of it, which luckily removed some of the mustard as well.
The soup (chicken and rice) was just as dull with no flavor aside from its acidity. The one good thing in it was the red quinoa, which was cooked perfectly and gave it a pleasant, grainy crunch. The white rice was just a cheap filler and did nothing to improve it. I think that a much better soup can be made from grains and veggies with chicken for about the same cost.
I must add that the gentlemen who was serving me was exceptionally polite and helpful and even ran after me to give me the baseball cap I had forgotten.
So maybe this restaurant has better items that I didn't get to try, but in my opinion, if you put something on the menu, you should make it worth tasting. Anyway, I wish them luck.<//text><Time>1474496252925< /Time>< gmap_id>

< UserId.>
100903848925934605912</UserId.>
<Text>Spice & Soul is a neat little restaurant that's off the uber-crowded beaten paths. We found ourselves there after being unable to find parking in Little Italy.

We had wanted pizza, but the pizza place across the street was closed, so Spice & Soul would have to do. We ordered a trio of appetizers: the tri-tip flat bread, the clucks and fries, and the hot mess fries.

The flat bread was fresh and light with a pesto aioli alongside mozzarella serving to cut the heaviness of the tri-tip. The clucks and fries were... Well, they were definitely chicken fingers and fries. Nothing much exciting there, though they were tasty.

The plate that stole the show for me was the hot mess fries. I had wanted it with brisket, but they were out, so I got pork instead. The fries came topped with mountains of meat and cheese. The pork was tender and smoked to perfection. Fantastic!

Spice & Soul gets a 4/5 with me. There was nothing objectionable about their food, but I found it all to lack dimension. I loved the hot mess fries, but it was still missing a little bit of zing or pizzazz to me, and the rest of the food was fine, but not great.

Absolutely check this place out if you're into craft beers, of which there are many, or if you're looking for some great smoked pork. Enjoy!</Text></record></dataset><record>

<GmapID>0x808e2e0856b84b19:0x4ff3d416d0f29794</GmapID>< text>
The Coyote Creek Parkway is a great place for a walk, run or a bike ride. The Parkway is approximately 15 miles long and runs from the north side of Morgan Hill near the Anderson Reservoir to Hellyer Lake in south San Jose. There are numerous bodies of water,  rest stops and wildlife to view. There was a small grass fire in early September, 2020, but the trail was not damaged (thank you firefighters!).< /text>

< user_id>
114188039371212819900<//user_id>
<user_name>Peter Estaniel<//user_name><date>1605228280735< /date>< Rate>
5</Rate>
<review>Love this trail! I ride from the Silver Creek staging area to the end of the trail in Morgan Hill, then back again. This stretch of the trail is beautiful and, for a good part of the distance, parallels the Coyote Creek.

For me, it's a pretty easy ride. The rolling hills aren't a problem if you have gears. After a rain, the creek tends to get pretty full, so beware of trail closures due to flooding. Keep in mind that the winds tend to blow northerly, so you'll most likely encounter a headwind when you ride back north. Last thing to note, there's not a whole lot of cover for much of the trail. During the summers, the sun is brutal. Plan accordingly.

If you're really adventurous, ride a another mile or so past the end of the trail in Morgan Hill and you'll get to Lake Anderson. Climb up the hill (it's short but demanding) and you'll get to see the reservoir.</review>< Pics>
None</Pics>
